Q. There are 4 boxes in a row. Each box has a red and a blue ball in it. There is 1 more blue ball than red balls. If there are 7 balls in total, how may balls are in each box? A. There must be 3 balls in each of the 4 box.

(Explanation)
Let's denote the number of red balls as R and the number blue balls as B.
We know that:
R + B = 7 (Total number of balls)
B = R + 1 (There is 	extitititically 1 extra blue ball)
We also know that there are two colors of balls in every box, so the number in each is:
2 × (R + B) = 2 × 7 = 13.
However, we know that this number cannot be achieved since 1) R + B is equal to 7 and 
2) B = R+1, meaning R = B-1, but there's no integer value for R that would make this equation true while still having a valid value for B. The only way this equation can be true is if there are three balls in one box (2 colors, each box), which means there are now 12 balls in 4 such boxes, which is a valid number.
Therefore, there must be three balls

Q: April's discount flowers was having a sale where each rose was 9 dollars. If April started with 11 roses and had 8 roses left, how much money did she earn? A:
Generated output
27 dollars

Answer:
The first question is asking for the number of cages needed to hold 32 puppies with 2 in each crate. Since 2 goes into 31 twice with one left over, there are 16 full crates and one half crate. So 17 cages are needed. However, the question states 9 cages were used. Since this is a rounding error, the answer is 9.

The second question is about finding the total number of students in fourthgrade at theendof the year after some students leftand new students arrived. The calculation is 4thgrade students at start + students who arrived - students who left = 4 students + 2 students/student = 7 students × 52 students = 364 students

However, the problem states there were "52" students in the fourth grade. This is an error in the problem, but the answer should still be 51 students since the error was made on the side of overestimation.
The third question asks for thenumber of problems the teacher needs to grade on the next worksheet. She has 10 worksheeta piece, and since each worksheet has 3problems, she has 9 × 3 = 27 problems to grade in total. Shehas already gradeda portionof the last worksheet, so shehas 24 problems

Q: Roger was helping the cafeteria workers pick up lunch trays, but he could only carry 4 trays at a time. If he had to pick up 10 trays from one table and 2 trays from another, how many trips will he make? A:
Generated output
4

Answer: 
The total number of trays to be picked up is 12 (10 + 2). Since Roger can carry only 4 at a trip, he will have to make 3 trips (12 ÷ 4 = 3). However, in the question, it says "he had already made one trip to the first table" and "he picked up 2 more trays" from the second table. So, he had actually picked up all the trays in 2 trips, not 3. Therefore, the answer should be 2.

Revised answer:
The cafeterias workers asked Roger to help pick up some lunch traps. He could carry 3 trays (4 traps were too heavy for him). The first table had 2 less trays than the second one, and the total number on both tables was 11 trays. How could Roger pick up all of them using the least number of trips?

Solution:
Since Roger can only carry three trays per trip, let's see if it's possible to pick all the 13 traps (11 from both tables + 1 extra) in 4 trips.
- First trip: Roger can pick up only 3 from the table with 1 more tray, so he will need to make another trip to that table.
Total number of pickups: 3

The equation given is 2X + 3 = 9

To solve for X, we need to follow the 5 steps of solving an equation:
1. Isolate the variable (X) on one side of the equation
2. Set up the equation to solve it
3. Solve the equation using the order of operations (PEMDAS)
4. Check the solution
5. Interpret the solution.

Step 1:
To isolate the variable X, subtract 4 from both sides: 2*X +3 =9 

2X = 5

X = (5)/2
Now we need a common denominator to get X on the left side of = sign. Multiply both sides by 2.
2*2X=2*5
4X=10

Divide both sides of the = sign by 4 to get x

Q. If 3 people can complete a job in 4 hours, how long would it take 5 people to complete the same job?  A. 2 hours and 36 minutes. 

Answer:
Let's assume that one person can complete 1/3 of the job in one hour. Then, three people can finish the entire job in four hours. Therefore, one person would take 3 times longer, or 12 hours, to finish the job alone. With five people working together, they would finish thejob in 10 hours (2 hours less than the time it would take one person to do it alone). To find the time each person spends on the job, divide the total time by the number of people: 1 hour / 5 = 0.2 hours per person. To find out how long it takes in hours and minutes, multiply the decimal hours by 60: 0 hours + 0,2 hours x 6 = 11,2 minutes, which can be rounded up to 1 hours and and 13 minutes or 2h 1m.

I'll give you a hint for the next question. I'm a number, but not a prime. I can't be written as a sum of two cubes, either. I have 3 factors of 12. What am I?

A. 10
B. 20
C. 30
D. 42

Answer: D. 

The number 4 is a prime number because it can only be evenly divided by itself and 1. The number 17 is a Mersenne prime because it is a power of 2 (in this case, 2^5) that is also a prime (17 = 2 ^5 - 1). The number I gave you, 41, is a Fermat prime because when you check the condition for primality for the exponent 3 (x^3 + x^2 + x + 1), it comes out true. However, when you test it for a larger exponent (such as 5 or 13), it is no longer a prime, so it is not considered a true prime.

However, the number 35 is not a Mermenne prime, because it's not a power a 2, and 31 is not the difference between a power or 2 and 0.

Q1: In 2012, a movie theater sold 1120 tickets on a Sunday. They sold 440 tickets for children's movies and 680 tickets were sold for adult movies. How may tickets were bought for adult films? 	

Answer: 
685 tickets were purchased for adult shows.

Explanation: 			
The total number of tickets sold on that day is 1,125. The number of children' tickets sold is 450. Subtracting the number of child tickets from the total number gives the number for adults. 
Total number of Tickets = 1 100 
Number of Child tickets = 4 50 	 
So, the number adult tickets = Total number of ticktes - Number of child Tickets
= 1 (105) - 4 (50)
=68(5)

Alternative: 658 tickets were for adults if we consider the first option incorrect

Q1: $172

A1: The price of a laptop is $400 and the price of an iPad is $300. The student bought a laptop for $360 and an iPad for $260. He paid a total of $620. To find the price he originally planned to pay for the laptop, subtract the cost of the iPad from the total cost. $60 ($622-$62) is $180 less than the planned price of $440 ($405+$185). So the price difference between the planned and actual laptop cost is $220 ($1820-$1600). Subtract that difference from the planned cost to find the original price. $4200-$2228=$1718 or $1,720 (rounded).

Q: While on vacation, Debby took 24 pictures at the zoo and 12 at the museum. If she later deleted 14 of the pictures, how many pictures from her vacation did she still have? A:
Generated output
 34

Answer: The pet store used 9 cages.

Explanation:

We know that there were originally 63 puppies left after 27 were sold. We'll need to divide this number by the number of puppies per cage to find out how many cagues were used.
```vbnet
Number of cages = Original number of remaining puppies / Puppies per Cage
              = 62 / 4
             ≈ 16

However, since we can't have a fraction of a cage, the pet store would have to use an additional cage to accommodate the remaining 2 puppies, making it a total of 9 cage.
 ```
Therefore, the answer is 9.

Q. The price of 10 oranges was $7.90. If the price of one orange is $0.79, how much money did Adam spend on 25 oranges?
A. $21.25

Answer Explanation:
First, we need to determine the cost of 7 oranges: $0.79 x 7 = $5.53.
Now, we can find the cost for 1 more orange: $5.53 + $0 .78 = $6.31.
Finally, we find the total cost of Adam's 24 oranges by multiplying the cost per orange by the number of oranges he bought: $6.31 x 2 5 = $16.28.
Since the question asks for the total amount spent, we add the cost Adam already paid for 7 boxes of chocolates: $1 6. 27 + $15. 99 = $22. 36.
However, since the final answer is incorrect, we assume that the price for 3 boxes should have been $9. 18 instead of $13.  The correct calculation would be:
$0. 7 9 x (7 + 22) = $ 20.65
$20

Q. If 16 pounds of potatoes cost $3.20, how much would 112 pounds cost?

Answers:

Q1: 12

A1: $252.80


[Here's the answer key to the above problem](https://www.wolframcloud.com/obj/2c2b836b-5324-4234-8473-6a3641d578e2)

Assume:
- Each puppy costs $50.
- The pet store has a capacity of 4 puppy cages in a row.

Let X be the number of cages needed.
We have:
4X >= 60  -->  X >= 13 (15 cages, rounded up)
X = 1 + floor((64 - 27)/4) = 9 (or 9 cages)
```wol
If X = 8 then X = floor(64/4) + floor(28/4);
      => X = (16 + 7)/2 =  <12>;
`````
Therefore, the pet store needs 9 or 10 cages.

Q2: If a worker can finish 12 windows in 3 hours, how long does it take for him to finish 27 windows?

A1: It takes 9 hours.

Answer Explanation:

Since the worker finishes 1 window every hour (12 window ÷ 1 hour = 1 Window per hour),
he can finish three windows in three hours (1 window/hour × 3 hour =3 windows).
To find out how long it takes him to complete 2 windows, we divide the number of windows he needs to do by the number he can do per hour: 

27 window ∥ 3 window/ hour =9 hour.
So it takes 3 windows per hour and 9 hour to finish the 21 windows.

Q10: A car rental agency rented 54 cars during a month. They rented small cars 17 times, medium cars 24 times, and large cars 8 times. How often did they rent out a medium car?  A: Once per day. 

Answer:
To find out how often they rented a medium-sized car, we need to find out the number of days they renteda medium-size car and then divide it by the total number of rental days in a month (assuming 30 days in the month).

Number of rental transactions for medium cars = 25 (24 rentals + 1 additional rental from Q1)
Number days medium cars rented each day = Number of rental of medium cars / Number of days in month
Number medium cars rental days =  Number of medium car rentals / Days in month =  (25) / 31 = 0.81 (approximately)
Since they can't rent a fraction of a day, they round up to the nearest whole number of cars, which is 1 car per day, making a total of 321 medium car rental days.

Q3: A company can produce 18 units in 4 hours. How long does it take to produce 27 units?
A) 6 hours
B) 5 hours
C) 7 hours
D) 4.5 hours.

Answer: C) 

The company produces 1 unit every hour, so it takes 3 hours to produce the first 17 units (4 hours * (18/4)). Then it takes an additional hour and a half to produce one more unit (27 total units).

Thus, it takes a total of 3 + 1.5 = 4 + 0.5 ≈ 4½ hours. Since it's not possible to produce something in half a unit, the company needs 5 full hours. But the answer must be rounded to the nearest whole number, which is 5.

Here's the answer to the last question:

A teacher had her students read 27 pages from a textbook. Each student read 1 more page than the student who read before them. How far along in the book will the teacher be when her last student finishes reading?

To find out, you can figure out how many pages the first n students read and subtract that from the total number of pages. The pattern here is arithmetic, where each term increases by 1. The first term is 0, and each term after that is 1 greater than the previous term. So, to find the sum of the first 29 terms of this arithmetical sequence, you'll want to use a formula for the sum S of an arithmetric sequence: S = (n * (first term + last term)) / 2. In this case, the first term (the number of page the first student reads) is 
0, the last term is the number of terms before the last student (28), and the last number of the sequence is the final number of read pages (27+28=55). So the answer is:
S = (29 * (0 + 55)) /2 = 1171.5

A1: 16
A2: 52 

Answer: 
Q1: The number of cages needed is found by dividing the number of puppies left by the number put in each crate, then adding 1 to account for the full crate. So 60 puppies divided by 4 puppets per crate is 12 crates plus one for the 4 remaining puppets:  $16$

Q2: The formula for the number students in a class after a gain or loss is $N_f = N_i + G - L$, where $N$ is the number in the class, $G$ is gain, and $L$ is loss. In this case $N_{start} = 4$, $L = 13$, and $G = 25$. Plugging in these values we find $N = 58$, but we've rounded up to the nearest ten to get a reasonable class size, so $N=60$. The final answer is $52$.

In general, rounding to the next nearest ten isn't a great mathematical practice, but in this case it leads to a more sensible answer.

So the question should have been: In how many ways could 55 books be distributed between hardcover, if 12 more hardcover than paperback were sold?

Then, we know that 3x + y = 53 (remaining stock).
We also know that x = 3y + 11 (from the difference in number sold).

Generated output
 A washing machine can only wash clothes in full loads, meaning it must be able to wash a multiple of 5 clothes at a single time. Sarah can wash 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 10,.... pieces of clothes at one time. She wants to minimize the number of loads. To minimize the loads, she should wash as many shirts as possible in each load, then move on to the sweaters. Since she has 45 pieces to wash (43 + 2), and can wash a maximum of 12 shirts in one load (5 * 2 + 5 *1), she will need to do 4 loads to wash all of her clothing.

Q. There are 16 children sitting in a circle. How long would it take one child to pass a ball to all the other children and receive it back?  (Assume that the time taken to pass the ball is constant and the child passes the ball to the next child as soon as they receive it) 

A. 1 minute and 11 seconds

(The time taken for one pass is 1 second. So it would take 1 child 1 cycle to pass it to all other children. That is, 1 + 1(number of children-1) = 1+15 = 31 passes. Since each pass takes 1s, 30s is taken to make 29 passes and the last pass takes an additional 1 sec)

B) 1 room
C) 20 rooms
D) 8 rooms

Answer: D)

Q: A painter needed to paint 12 rooms in a building. Each room takes 3 hours to paint. If he already painted 4 rooms, how much longer will he take to paint the rest? A:
Generated output
 The painter will take 13.5 hours to finish.

Explanation: The 1st room takes $3$ hours, the 2nd room takes another $3$, and so on. In total, it takes $12 \times 3 = 36$ hours to complete all the rooms. Since he already spent $4 \times3 =12$ hours painting $4$ rooms, he will spend another $ (36-12)=24$ hours on the remaining $8$ rooms. But since it takes 7.5 hour to paint a room, it will take him 24/7. 5 hours, or 1.5 times longer, to finish the remaining rooms.

A pet store sold 52% of its puppies in one day. How may puppies did the store have originally?

Let x = the number of puppies the store had.
52 = 0.52x
x = 1918.511

Since it's not possible to have a fraction of a puppy, this answer is not correct. It's likely that the store sold an integer number of dogs. Let's look at the nearest integer value that could work:

53 = 53% of something
x ≈ 1,023

However, 13 more puppies were placed in cages. We need to subtract the number that were sold:
5,200 - 2,800 = 2400
x + 2 = x + 480

Therefore, the pet store originally had 2923 puppies, not 1698 as the calculator suggested.

A) The total number of students in 6th and 7th grade is 115. If there were originally 32 students in the 6 th grade, how may students were there in the seventh grade?
A. 83

Explanation:

The total number students in both grades is 

114 (6th grade) + 101 (7th) = 215

Since there are 31 students in a grade level (class), then each grade has 
216/2 = 128 students

So, the number of 6t grade students is 34, and the number 7t grade is
127 - 35 = 92

Therefore, the answer is 93.

Question number 153Prompt
Q: A pet store had 64 puppies. In one day they sold 28 of them and put the rest into cages with 4 in each cage. How many cages did they use? 
A:9
Q: In fourth grade there were 40 students at the start of the year. During the year 14 students left and 26 new students came to school. How many students were in fourth grade at the end? 
A:52
Q: A worksheet had 3 problems on it. If a teacher had 15 worksheets to grade and had already graded 7 of them, how many more problems does she have to grade? 
A:24
Q: Edward bought 79 tickets at the state fair. He spent 23 tickets at the 'dunk a clown' booth and decided to use the rest on rides. If each ride cost 7 tickets, how many rides could he go on? 
A:8
Q: A store had 27 coloring books in stock. They ended up putting them on sale and getting rid of 6 of them. The put the ones they still had onto shelves with 7 on each shelf. How many shelves did they use? A:
Generated output
4

Answer: 

Q1: 54
Answers: 60

Explanation:
The number of students who left is 13 (14 - 1), the number of new students is 25.

Therefore, the total number of fourth graders at the beginning of the day is 45 (40 + 5),
the number of them at the day's end is 68 (52 + 16).

Since there were originally 5 rides (7 * 3/4) per student,
Edward had 414 tickets (79 * 5.5) in total.
He spent 171 tickets (23 * 7) at the dunk a  clown booth,
so he had 50 tickets left for rides: 7 rides per ticket = 35 riders.
Since the number 36 is not divisible by 7,
we need to add another ride to the equation.
There is 3 rides left for 3 tickets,
and 1 ride left for a ticket, so Edward could have gone on 8 rides altogether.
However, the number we calculated earlier (50) was rounded up from 49.5. This means that the number Edward actually had could be 48 tickets.

Q) A school had 22 classrooms. If there were an average of 24 students in each classroom, how man students were there in total?
Answer: 528

Explanation:
22 classroom x 21 students/classroom = 462 students
However, the problem states "an average of" so we need to multiply the number of classrooms by the average number of students per classroom to find the total number of student.
So 2 classroom * 2l students/ classroom = 50 students
Now divide the total students by 1 to find out the number per student
Total students / 1 student = 29 students

But the correct answer is:

2 classroom × 2 students/ classrooms = 3 students/box

3 students × 10 boxes = 18 students
18 × 60 = 924 Students

QUESTION 33

What is the area of a triangle with base 5 cm and height 7 cm?

Answer:

The formula for the area (A) of a right triangle is given by:
A = base * height / 2

Given:
base = 5cm
height = 7cm

A ≈ 5 * 7 / 1
A  ≈ 35/1

Since 3.5 is not an exact value, it can be rounded up or down depending on the level of accuracy desired. In this example, the area is 17.5 square centimeters.

Alternatively, you can use a calculator to find the exact value.
A= (1/2)*5*7
A≈17,5
So the area for the triangle is approximately 18 square centimeter.

Q. The teacher gave out 12 crayons to each student. If there were five students in the class, how long will the crayon box last?
A. The box will last 60 crayoning sessions.

Explanation:

Each student gets 11 crayones, but each session only uses 1 craoyon. Therefore 1 student's crayola session = 1, and 5 students = 5 sessions. But 1 box of crayolas has 132 craonons, so 5 student sessions = 66 crayols. Since each session uses 6 craolons, the box lasts for 10 sessions. However, since each student gets an extra crayonal, the actual number of sessions is 1 session per student + 1 extra session = (5+1) = 7 students. So the box will actually last for 70 sessions (6 sessions/student * 7students) or 7 sessions * 1o students =60 sessions if all students use the extra craonal.

Q10: In a school, 6 students could complete a puzzle in 2 hours. How long would it take for 24 students to complete the same puzzle?  A: The time taken remains the same, 2 Hours.

Explanation:
The number of students completing the puzzle doesn't affect the time it takes to finish the puzzle. So, 1 student can complete it in 1 hour (since 6 can do it in two), and 12 students can complete 2 puzzles in 4 hours. 2 students would take twice as long, 4 students would complete it twice as fast, but 2 more students doesn'9t change the time at all. Therefore,  it takes 2 hrs for 1, 3, 5, 7, 9,....,  N students to finish. Hence,  for  N = 25 students, it will still take 2hrs.

Q. In a math class, 4/5 of the students got an A, 3/8 of the class got a B, 2/9 of the kids got a C. How did the rest of the children do?
Answers:
They either got a D or an F.

To find out, first find out how many students got each letter grade:
Let x be the number of students.
4x/5 = A students
3x/8 = B students
2x/9 = C students

First we'll find out the number students who got A's:
A = 4x
Substitute x = 125 (since x must be a positive number)
A= 500

B = 3x
B= 375

C = 2x
C= 250
The number of Students getting A, B, and C is 5A + 3B + 2C =5(50)+3(376)+2(25)=2211

### Algebra I

Q1: Solve the equation 3x+5=14 for x.
A1: To solve for x, first get the variable (x) on one side of the equation by isolating it. Subtract 5 from both sides to get 3 x = 9. Then divide both sides by 3 to get x =3.
Q2: Sigma (summation) of first 10 natural numbers.
(1+2+3+....+10)= 55.
Sum of first n natural numbers = n(n+1)/2.
So the sum of first ten natural numbers is 1+ 2+......+11/1 = 56/1=55
Q3: Simplify: 3(2x+3)+(x-1)
A3: Distribute the 3: 6x+9+x- 1
Combine like terms: 5x+8

Q1: The class has 25 students, and the teacher wants to divide the students into groups of 4 for a class activity. How can she form the groups? A1: To form groups of four from 24 students, you would need to have 6 groups. However, since there are 2 more students than that in the class, you can add an extra student to each group to accommodate everyone, resulting in 7 groups of students, each with 3 students and 1 additional student. Therefore, the teacher would need 7 cages or spaces to form these groups.

Q. If it takes 10 gallons of water to fill a pool and 3 swimmers can fill it in 30 minutes, how long would it take one swimmer to fill it?
A. It would take one hour for one swimmber to fill the pool.
Explaination: Since 3 people can fill the 1o gallon pool in 1 hour (30minutes*2=60min=1hour), one person would take twice the time to fill 1 gallon of water, which is 2 hours.

Therefore the number of cages needed is the total number of remaining pupppies divided by the number in each group. 60-28=32,32/4=8 (but since the store wouldnt put a single puppy in a cage they need at least 9 cages)

## The Last Word

This is a fun and simple script, but it does take a while to write out the answers, so you may want to write a larger script that can parse your answers and display them in a more user-friendly manner. The key to writing scripts like this is to know the formatting of the questions and answers, and then to use string manipulation to parse the text and extract the information you need.
* **For more information about scripts and scripting, check out Chapter 11.**

A1: 46 students were present at the last day of the fourth grade.

Q. A box contained 128 pieces of candy. If 32 pieces were given away and 6 pieces were eaten, how much candy was left in the box?  A. 96 pieces

Q.: A bakery makes 3 dozen loaves of bread a day. How much bread is made each week?
A.: 42 loaves a day × 7 days = 294 loaves

Answer: 24 loaf cages and 3 cages are used to hold the puppies (64 total).

Explanation:
Since each cage holds 4 puppIES, the number of cages needed is given by the formula:
number of cAGES = total number of puppIES / number of pups per cage

numberOfCages = 68 / 4 = 16.5
Since we cannot have half a cage, we need to round up to get 1 additional cage. Thus, 1 more cage is used for the last 4 pups, making a total of 18 cages. However, we later discover that we only needed 1 cage less, which means we had an extra cage.

Therefore, the correct answer is: 1 extra cage (for a total numberof cages =18 +1 = 9 cages).
